--- Commit Message ---
LU-16159 lod: cancel update llogs upon recovery abort

If recovery is aborted, cancel update catalog from catlist, and keep
them on disk for some time (for debug purpose), as can avoid
accumulating stale update records, and also avoid recovery problems
if update llogs are corrupt.

Update llogs are canceled after recovery completes and before regular
request processing. For these logs, their ctime will be set, and log
header will be marked with LLOG_F_MAX_AGE|LLOG_F_RM_ON_ERR, and when
30 days passed, they will be removed automatically.

Tidy up recovery abort code:
* if obd_abort_recovery is set, or OBD is stopping, stop both
  client recovery and MDT recovery.
* otherwise if obd_abort_mdt_recovery is set, stop MDT recovery only.

lctl llog_print support printing update log FIDs used by specified
MDT:
* "lctl --device <MDT> llog_print update_log" will list all update
  llog FIDs used by this MDT device.

Disabled replay-single.sh 100c stripe check because abort_recovery
will cancel update llogs, and won't replay them upon next recovery.

Added replay-single.sh 100d.

Formatall in the end of replay-single.sh because directory unlink may
fail.

Test-Parameters: mdscount=2 mdtcount=4 testlist=replay-single,replay-single,replay-single,replay-single,replay-single,replay-single,replay-single,replay-single,replay-single

 > %% THIS TEST SESSION CRASHED %%

Looks like this triggered an internal LASSERT() in the llog code:

  == replay-single test complete, duration 14588 sec
  dt_object.h:2296:dt_declare_record_write()) ASSERTION( dt->do_body_ops ) failed: [0x2c0005223:0x4:0x0] doesn't exit

Presumably the error message should be "doesn't exist".  We shouldn't LASSERT() on data from the filesystem, so it looks like the error handling here needs to be improved.

--- Message (Mikhail Pershin, 2022-10-25 11:22:47.000000000) ---
Patch Set 13:

> "In case the system is stuck in recovery, while user wants to get system up ASAP, and run "lctl abort_recovery", then there is no way to know what went wrong."
My point is that while it worth to keep files, I don't think LOD should do all related GC. For me that is LFSCK job to do. More widely, LFCKS should determine all orphaned plain llogs and delete them (e.g. if user just truncated catalog without taking care about plain llogs in it)

--- Message (Lai Siyao, 2022-10-25 15:01:21.000000000) ---
Patch Set 13:

> Patch Set 13:
> 
> > "In case the system is stuck in recovery, while user wants to get system up ASAP, and run "lctl abort_recovery", then there is no way to know what went wrong."
> My point is that while it worth to keep files, I don't think LOD should do all related GC. For me that is LFSCK job to do. More widely, LFCKS should determine all orphaned plain llogs and delete them (e.g. if user just truncated catalog without taking care about plain llogs in it)

But for best practice,LFSCK should be run after recovery abort in case it left some files/dirs not able to access (maybe this should be done automatically after recovery complete). Now ctime is set on canceled logs, and LLOG_F_RM_ON_ERR set in log headers upon cancel, stale llogs are reclaimed at MDT start, which is similar to orphan cleanup.

--- Message (Lai Siyao, 2022-10-28 09:24:05.000000000) ---
Patch Set 14:

> Patch Set 14:
> 
> Well, it looks OK but I have more questions about managing stale llogs. Whole idea to keep them for some time is based on fact that someone would need to gather them, how that could be done? After unlinking from catalog, orphaned plain llogs can be found by LLOG_F_MAX_AGE flag I suppose and 'lctl llog_print' is the tool to list all of them. So,
> 1) does it indicate somehow that plain llog is 'stale'? I don't see that in code.

'lctl llog_print' will list update logs in use. lod_prepare()->lod_update_log_gc() will reclaim stale update logs.

> 2) if there were more than one cases with llog cleanup, then we would have several sets of stale plain llogs, how to distinguish one set from another? I suppose by their ctime?

Yes, ctime can be used to distinguish different set, and llog_cancel_cb() will print messages in console too.

> 3) wouldn't that be better to just replace whole catalog llog at once in catalog index "update_log_dir" so we will have 'stale' catalog with all plain llogs still referenced in it? In that all llog tree can be analysed starting from catalog and also corruptions in catalog could be seen

Yes, this will have the same effect, but the code is more complex. Is corrupt catalog seen before? catalog creation and new log record write are in sync mode.

>'lctl llog_print' will list update logs in use. lod_prepare()
> lod_update_log_gc() will reclaim stale update logs.
> llog_cancel_cb() will print messages in console too.
Well, we are keeping stale logs only for one reason - someone will gather them later for analysis. Therefore this patch should provide practical way to do that. One time message in console is neither practical nor good - some can be just skipped with "Skipping 1234 similar messages", can't they? We need a way to show all stale llogs grouped by ctime at any time we need that, something like 'lctl llog_print --stale', or via procfs, or script/tool to list them on server. A lot of work is done in Lustre code to save such logs for analysis but to make that analysis possible we provide just one time message in console.

> Yes, this will have the same effect, but the code is more complex. Is > corrupt catalog seen before? catalog creation and new log record write > are in sync mode.
That is not critical if code will be more complex. But in general, yes, sometimes there are empty records in update log catalog after failover and I tend to think this issue is not fixes yet in code. LU-16203 is about to handle such records but reason is still unclear.

--- Message (Andreas Dilger, 2022-10-29 06:33:35.000000000) ---
Patch Set 14:

Mike, my thought here is that automatic llog removal on abort_recov_mdt reduces the problems seen by the admins and gets their system working again with the least effort after recovery has already failed. 

I agree that preventing recovery failure in the first place is also important, and we've made a number of fixes in that area already.  Having the actual llogs also helps debug such problems after they are hit, though in some cases it may be enough that the system is up and running again. 

I think it would be reasonable to go ahead with this patch (once it is passing testing), and have a second patch that can automatically collect the logs after such a problem is hit. 

We typically get a showall that dumps the console log messages, so it would be up to us to see the LCONSOLE_INFO() messages and request the llogs be saved.  We would have 30 days to collect them after a failure. This could be done from user space with a modified version of your cleanup script to use debugfs dump so they can be collected from the running MDT to avoid a system outage to mount as ldiskfs.

The failure is as below:
1. an operation on MDT1 modifies objects on MDT0 and MDT1, and it's not committed.
2. MDT0 is restarted for 3 times (in test 100d), and it hasn't connected to MDT1 yet.
3. MDT1 is stopped, but the request in step 1 is in delay list, which cause system hung in ptlrpc_invalidate_import().

When I change restart to only 1 time in test 100d, the issue looks gone.
